1c9cb 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
1cb06 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
1cc96 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1cd4e GPIB status vector:
1cd63 status[0] - Device Clear State
1cd82  status[1] - Device Trigger State
1cda4  status[2] - Listener Active State
1cdc8 status[3] - Talker Active State
1cde9 status[4] - Attention line asserted
1ce0e status[5] -
1ce1a Controller In Charge
1ce2f  status[6] - Remote State
1ce49  status[7] - Lockout State
1ce65 status[8] - I/O Completed 
1ce81 status[9] - not used
1ce96  status[10]- not used
1ceac  status[11]- not used
1cec3 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
1ceeb status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
1cf0b  status[14]- Timeout occured
1cf28  status[15]- GPIB error detected
1cf4c GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1cf81 GPIB Error:
1cf92 -No error
1cfa1 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
1cfc8 -No listeners detected on write
1cfed -Controller not addressed correctly
1d016 -Invalid argument(s)
1d031 (perhaps bad address string????)
1d057 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
1d07d -I/O operation aborted
1d099 -hardware not present
1d0b4 -DMA error
1d0c4 -DMA bus timeout
1d0da -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
1d101 progress
1d10f -function not implemented
1d12e -file system error
1d146 -shareable board exclusively owned
1d16e -GPIB bus error (commands)
1d18e -Serial Poll Byte Lost
1d1aa -SRQ line cannot be cleared
1d1cb -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
1d225 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
1d373 GPIB status vector:
1d388 status[0] - Device Clear State
1d3a7  status[1] - Device Trigger State
1d3c9  status[2] - Listener Active State
1d3ed status[3] - Talker Active State
1d40e status[4] - Attention line asserted
1d433 status[5] -
1d43f Controller In Charge
1d454  status[6] - Remote State
1d46e  status[7] - Lockout State
1d48a status[8] - I/O Completed 
1d4a6 status[9] - not used
1d4bb  status[10]- not used
1d4d1  status[11]- not used
1d4e8 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
1d510 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
1d530  status[14]- Timeout occured
1d54d  status[15]- GPIB error detectedA=data string contains count data bytes from the GPIB device.

2b172 LVINLBVWc(
2b185 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set. 
2b1bb GPIB Error:
2b1cc -No error
2b1db -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
2b202 -No listeners detected on write
2b227 -Controller not addressed correctly
2b250 -Invalid argument(s)
2b26b (perhaps bad address string????)
2b291 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
2b2b7 -I/O operation aborted
2b2d3 -hardware not present
2b2ee -DMA error
2b2fe -DMA bus timeout
2b314 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
2b33b progress
2b349 -function not implemented
2b368 -file system error
2b380 -shareable board exclusively owned
2b3a8 -GPIB bus error (commands)
2b3c8 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
2b3e4 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
2b405 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
2b461 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
2b519 GPIB status vector:
2b52e status[0] - Device Clear State
2b54d  status[1] - Device Trigger State
2b56f  status[2] - Listener Active State
2b593 status[3] - Talker Active State
2b5b4 status[4] - Attention line asserted
2b5d9 status[5] -
2b5e5 Controller In Charge
2b5fa  status[6] - Remote State
2b614  status[7] - Lockout State
2b630 status[8] - I/O Completed 
2b64c status[9] - not used
2b661  status[10]- not used
2b677  status[11]- not used
2b68e status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
2b6b6 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
2b6d6  status[14]- Timeout occured
2b6f3  status[15]- GPIB error detected
2b715 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
2b812 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
2b948 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
2b9b9   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
2b9e9  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
2ba18  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device. 
2ba94 GPIB status vector:
2baa9 status[0] - Device Clear State
2bac8  status[1] - Device Trigger State
2baea  status[2] - Listener Active State
2bb0e status[3] - Talker Active State
2bb2f status[4] - Attention line asserted
2bb54 status[5] -
2bb60 Controller In Charge
2bb75  status[6] - Remote State
2bb8f  status[7] - Lockout State
2bbab status[8] - I/O Completed 
2bbc7 status[9] - not used
2bbdc  status[10]- not used
2bbf2  status[11]- not used
2bc09 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
2bc31 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
2bc51  status[14]- Timeout occured
2bc6e  status[15]- GPIB error detected

6958a /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
696be Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
697d2 VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
6992b True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

6c50c Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.

746b5 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
747b1 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram. 7490a      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
7493e      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
74978      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
749b1      error, and a positive value is a warning.

74a13      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

8f922 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.$

99520 (I32) 
99527 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
99623 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
9977c      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
997b0      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
997ea      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
99823      error, and a positive value is a warning.
99853      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
99885      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
998b6 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

99960 (ABC) 
99967 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
99a1e f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
99b20      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
99b53      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
99b82      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
99bbc      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
99bf5      error, and a positive value is a warning.
99c25      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
99c54      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
99c85 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

b41b3 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
b430c      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b4340      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
b437a      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
b43b3      error, and a positive value is a warning.
b43e3      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
b4415      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
b4446 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b44d2 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
b45b8 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
b45e7 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
b4606 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
b4640 Optional Parameter Default Values:
b4663     bd - GPIB board (0)
b467b     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
b46a4     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
b46d1     logical addr - VXI logical address 
b46fa EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.

c45b4 VISA session (for class)
c45d5 This VI loads the addressing information about the instrument into the Open VXI Instrument VI and returns the instrument ID.  You can reset the instrument by setting the front panel reset control.  You must run this VI before using any of the instrument driver VIs for this instrument.
c46f5 (I32) 
c46fc A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
c47f7 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
c48f9      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
c492c      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
c495b      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
c4995      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
c49ce      error, and a positive value is a warning.
c49fe      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
c4a2d      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
c4a60 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
c4ac5 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
c4b2d The code input identifies the error or warning.
c4b5e The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
c4bc6 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
c4c07 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
c4c71 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
c4dca      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
c4dfe      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
c4e38      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
c4e71      error, and a positive value is a warning.
c4ea1      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
c4ed3      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
c4f06 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
c4f6b The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
c4fd3 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
c5014 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
c507c The code input identifies the error or warning.
c50ad The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

ccacb The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
ccb4b You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
ccc2a Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
cccb1 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.
ccd38 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
ccdeb The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
cce46 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
ccf30 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
ccfb8 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.
cd03f 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

dc351 VFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
dc3bb This VI writes the value in pattern to the port identified by task ID.
dc403 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.84(u32) task ID: identifies the group and I/O pattern.D@(u32) pattern: specifies the new state of the lines in the port.
dc523 x(i32) line mask: determines which lines in the port the write affects. If you set line mask to -1, the VI writes to the entire port and sets all the lines in the port to the states specified by the bits in pattern. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI changes only line n in the port to the state that bit n of pattern specifies. The default setting for line mask is -1.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.
dc6d3 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information. e38be This VI reads the port identified by task ID and returns the pattern read.
e390a See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
e39b3 (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

eb21b For most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
eb284 This VI establishes a port configuration. You can use the task ID that this VI returns only in digital port VIs.
eb2f6 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
eb403 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
eb4a8 When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
eb636 ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
eb878 (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
eb907 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
eb9cf      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
eba03      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
eba3d      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
eba77      error, and a positive value is a warning.
ebaa7      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
ebad9      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
ebb0a xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
ebb83 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module.
ebcca (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
ebdba (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
ebf13      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
ebf47      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
ebf81      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
ebfbb      error, and a positive value is a warning.
ebfeb      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
ec01d      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
ec04e 1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
ec07f (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

105528  INSTRUCTIONS:
105538 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
105830 Other Uses:
10583e local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1059ba user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
105abb exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
105cf9 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

106531 GetCommErr"
106551 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
106786 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
106831 displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
1068a4 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
10692b displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
1069c4 HDcode out is the error code indicated by the error in or error code.
106a0a b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
106a6c error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
106b0b user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
106be7 user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
106cc1 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
106cf1 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
106d6e error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
106dff exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
106ec3 (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
106f02 cancels error under the following conditions:
106f32 If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
107086 sets error under the following conditions:
1070b3 If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
1071ec jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
107256 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
107304 51code is the error code associated with an error.
107339 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1073d2 |xerror out contains the same information as status out, code out, and source out. It has the same structure as error in.
10744e status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
1074fc 51code is the error code associated with an error.
107531 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1075ca mimessage describes the error code that occurred, the source of the error, and a description of the error.

11451a device
114528 port number@
114537 pattern
114542 port width (8)
114554 iteration (0:initialize)
11457c Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
11462f The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
11468a You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
114774 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
1147fc Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1148f5 &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
114995 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
114b1e (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
114bb8 M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
114d09 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

11b119 pattern
11b124 iteration (0:initialize)
11b14c Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
11b1ff The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
11b27f You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
11b35e Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
11b3e5 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
11b4dd =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
11b594 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
11b71d (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
11b7b6 J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
11b904 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.
